<div id="review_2483287460" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2483287460" />
    <a title="Tim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7202176-tim"><img alt="Tim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1324164999p2/7202176.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2483287460?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tim" href="/user/show/7202176-tim">Tim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780752879581" href="/book/show/1727319.The_Killer_Inside_Me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7202176-tim?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7202176-tim?shelf=1950s">1950s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7202176-tim?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7202176-tim?shelf=mystery-crime">mystery-crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2483287460" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7380762104952669081"><i>"A weed is a plant out of place."</i><br/><br/>Indulge me for a moment; before I talk about the book’s contents, let me talk about the physical book. The cover of my edition is a plain tan-ish color, with just the title, the author, a few small pictures of sheriff stars, revolvers and bottles lined in a row and then a quote of praise that takes up about a third of the cover. The quote is as follows:<br/><br/>“Probably the most chilling and believable first-person story of a criminally warped mind I have ever encountere</span>
  <span id="freeText7380762104952669081" style="display:none"><i>"A weed is a plant out of place."</i><br /><br />Indulge me for a moment; before I talk about the book’s contents, let me talk about the physical book. The cover of my edition is a plain tan-ish color, with just the title, the author, a few small pictures of sheriff stars, revolvers and bottles lined in a row and then a quote of praise that takes up about a third of the cover. The quote is as follows:<br /><br />“Probably the most chilling and believable first-person story of a criminally warped mind I have ever encountered.” <br />- Stanley Kubrick<br /><br />If you have ever seen Kubrick’s films (almost all based on novels), you would know that’s actually saying quite a bit. <br /><br />This is the story of Lou Ford. He’s a good old boy, a southern gentleman, filled with corny “words of wisdom” like “the grass is always greener on the other side” and such. He’s a deputy in a little place known as Central City, and it’s the perfect job for him, as it allows him easier access to cover up his crimes. You see despite Lou’s slow-witted façade, he’s quite the clever murderer. <br /><br /><i>"I tried to be extra pleasant to her. She was getting on my nerves, hanging around so much. But she wouldn't be hanging around long, so I thought I ought to be as nice as I could."</i><br /><br />These are our narrator's thoughts about his girlfriend who he plans on killing. Ladies and gentlemen, this book starts off classic noir and moves straight into horror territory. We get a detailed account of Lou’s actions, and though it’s somewhat ridiculous of me to say this given other works at the time, but I was genuinely shocked that this was published in 1952. This feels… grittier, darker, something I would expect more out of an author in the 70s who wanted to mirror stylistic touches from the past. The book is violent and doesn’t shy away from its sexual content either (though playing a careful balance as to never go quite too far). <br /><br />Lou is easily one of the most disturbing protagonists I’ve ever read. He smiles and acts the fool to people, all of them knowing what a big soft hearted fellow he is, all while planning out what he is going to do next. He often tries to justify his actions, trying to make the reader sympathetic towards him. He’s constantly making excuses and then making new ones when those don’t seem to pan out for him. It’s someone else’s fault always… not good old Lou’s. Obviously it was his childhood, or maybe was his father, or maybe it's the way society acts, or maybe all of the above. You understand don’t you? Lou’s a nice guy, right?<br /><br />It’s absolutely <i>chilling</i>, and worst of all is that you occasionally get the impression that he truly does like some of these people, and well, it’s just such a gosh darn shame that things had to end up like this. <br /><br /><i>"I grinned, feeling a little sorry for him. It was funny the way these people kept asking for it. Just latching onto you, no matter how you tried to brush them off, and almost telling you how they wanted it done. Why'd they all have to come to me to get killed? Why couldn't they kill themselves?"</i><br /><br />This is a masterfully done novel. A work of fiction that gets under the reader’s skin with a smile and a laugh. It is also a shockingly funny novel, which makes it even more uncomfortable, as you see how easy it is for Lou to disarm people. When he’s not acting like a fool, he’s quick witted and borderline charming. This managed to creep me out in a way <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28676.American_Psycho" title="American Psycho by Bret Easton Ellis" rel="nofollow noopener">American Psycho</a> never did, as unlike Bateman, I found myself sometimes liking Lou.<br /><br />And that dear readers, is truly a frightening thing.<br /><br />A well deserved 4 out of 5 stars and a full recommendation. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7380762104952669081" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/744551077?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mara" href="/user/show/1923002-mara">Mara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1923002-mara?shelf=recommended-to-me">recommended-to-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1923002-mara?shelf=2014-reads">2014-reads</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer744551077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12352160288866756025">I've read what some may consider to be a creepy number of non-fiction books on sociopathy (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/72536.The_Sociopath_Next_Door' title='The Sociopath Next Door by Martha Stout' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Sociopath Next Door</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/132615.Snakes_in_Suits_When_Psychopaths_Go_to_Work' title='Snakes in Suits When Psychopaths Go to Work by Paul Babiak' rel='nofollow noopener'>Snakes in Suits: When Psychopaths Go to Work</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/661059.The_Mask_of_Sanity' title='The Mask of Sanity by Hervey M. Cleckley' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Mask of Sanity</a>). All of them attempt to offer insight into the heads of these individuals among us who exist without conscience, and adeptly "play human." Many of them (especially <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/56465.The_Gift_of_Fear_Survival_Signals_That_Protect_Us_from_Violence' title='The Gift of Fear Survival Signals That Protect Us from Violence by Gavin de Becker' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Gift of Fear: Survival Signals That Protect Us from Violence</a> by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/31933.Gavin_de_Becker' title='Gavin de Becker' rel='nofollow noopener'>Gavin de Becker</a> - which rumor has it Oprah recommended) try to aid the average, non-so</span>
  <span id="freeText12352160288866756025" style="display:none">I've read what some may consider to be a creepy number of non-fiction books on sociopathy (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/72536.The_Sociopath_Next_Door" title="The Sociopath Next Door by Martha Stout" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sociopath Next Door</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/132615.Snakes_in_Suits_When_Psychopaths_Go_to_Work" title="Snakes in Suits When Psychopaths Go to Work by Paul Babiak" rel="nofollow noopener">Snakes in Suits: When Psychopaths Go to Work</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/661059.The_Mask_of_Sanity" title="The Mask of Sanity by Hervey M. Cleckley" rel="nofollow noopener">The Mask of Sanity</a>). All of them attempt to offer insight into the heads of these individuals among us who exist without conscience, and adeptly "play human." Many of them (especially <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/56465.The_Gift_of_Fear_Survival_Signals_That_Protect_Us_from_Violence" title="The Gift of Fear Survival Signals That Protect Us from Violence by Gavin de Becker" rel="nofollow noopener">The Gift of Fear: Survival Signals That Protect Us from Violence</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/31933.Gavin_de_Becker" title="Gavin de Becker" rel="nofollow noopener">Gavin de Becker</a> - which rumor has it Oprah recommended) try to aid the average, non-sociopathic Joe in identifying and avoiding such individuals. The crux of the advice being that there's just this kind of gut feeling that you ought to go with. Jim Thompson, however, lets you climb into the brain of your neighborhood sociopath and does so in a way that is just so satisfying. <br /><br />Lou Ford, deputy sheriff and creep extraordinaire is playing a game with the world around him. <br /><blockquote>That’s what I was going to be; I was going to have to live and get along with rubes. I wasn’t ever going to have anything but some safe, small job, and I’d have to act accordingly.</blockquote><br />He bores people with platitudes just to watch them squirm, and (maybe I shouldn't be admitting this) I couldn't help but laugh with him as he did so. This book is a heaping spoonful of sick satisfaction...and I loved it. </span>

<div id="review_854920167" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/854920167?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer854920167" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2102324437705786405">This is a slightly tricky book to rate and review. I want to give at least a minor warning as I think some readers will find the book to some extent disturbing. that said it's considered a classic of it's type and I can see why. The writing could be called masterful.<br/><br/>This novel was written in 1952. Other than a few terms that are obsolete the story holds up well and in no way really feels dated. I mean yeah we have older cars, limited phone availability and a '50s society but it doesn't "jump out</span>
  <span id="freeText2102324437705786405" style="display:none">This is a slightly tricky book to rate and review. I want to give at least a minor warning as I think some readers will find the book to some extent disturbing. that said it's considered a classic of it's type and I can see why. The writing could be called masterful.<br /><br />This novel was written in 1952. Other than a few terms that are obsolete the story holds up well and in no way really feels dated. I mean yeah we have older cars, limited phone availability and a '50s society but it doesn't "jump out" or in any way intrude into the storytelling/reading. <br /><br />As a side note there is a 2010 movie adaption of this book. I have never seen it so I can't comment on it. I do know the movie was roundly criticized for violence against women. As I said I haven't seen the movie, but if the movie stays true to the book there's no way to avoid that.<br /><br />Lou Ford is somewhat of a psychopathic sadist. The book is told from Lou's point of view and the most frightening thing about it is Lou's voice. He's so normal and everybody likes him. Lou on the other hand has known all along about the monster that's imprisoned inside him, he's struggled to keep it there. He's been careful for years to keep it chained. The book will take us on a guided tour of Lou's descent into madness. We get a front row seat to his mind. He moves among his friends, his neighbors and no one knows who...or what he really is.<br /><br />None of that^ is a spoiler, but I can't say anymore without a spoiler. I don't want to do that. I do want you to know however that you'll get some graphic violence (still not as graphic as some more modern books but it gets the job done). It's emotionally straining and emotionally draining but it's extremely well written.<br /><br />I can recommend it with certain reservations. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2102324437705786405" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13031471967365149128">4.5 stars. <br/>Imagine if Mayberry's Sheriff Andy Taylor was secretly a serial killer and you will have a good idea of what you are getting into with this novel. <br/>This one is hard for me to rate. Just going by how I felt when reading it, I felt it was a solid 4. I really enjoyed it, although I felt it started slowing down just a touch near the end (although the ending itself was fantastic). I have to give it extra points, though, because Thompson's craft is absolutely incredible. He totally nails the</span>
  <span id="freeText13031471967365149128" style="display:none">4.5 stars. <br />Imagine if Mayberry's Sheriff Andy Taylor was secretly a serial killer and you will have a good idea of what you are getting into with this novel. <br />This one is hard for me to rate. Just going by how I felt when reading it, I felt it was a solid 4. I really enjoyed it, although I felt it started slowing down just a touch near the end (although the ending itself was fantastic). I have to give it extra points, though, because Thompson's craft is absolutely incredible. He totally nails the "murder mystery from the murderer's point of view" story. Also, as the story progresses and the main character's mind starts deteriorating, you can actually feel this breakdown happening. You literally follow the main character into the jaws of madness. <br /><br />As far as I can remember, this is my first Jim Thompson novel. Based on the strength of this one book, however, I went and picked up a bunch of his other novels. Anyone who likes <i>American Psycho</i> or noir should definitely pick this book up. <br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_15237429" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/15237429" />
    <a title="Nancy Oakes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/900340-nancy-oakes"><img alt="Nancy Oakes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507555979p2/900340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/15237429?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nancy Oakes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nancy Oakes" href="/user/show/900340-nancy-oakes">Nancy Oakes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/900340-nancy-oakes?shelf=crime-fiction">crime-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/900340-nancy-oakes?shelf=crime-fiction-america">crime-fiction-america</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer15237429" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15104659426266499800">The Killer Inside Me is one of those novels that needs no introduction at all -- it is and will always be a classic of American noir fiction, it's been made into two movies (1976 and 2010), and chances are that if you haven't read the novel you've at least seen the film. Or, if you're really fainthearted, you've experienced neither, since both book and movie are dark, disturbing, and well past the point of unsettling. It's also one of those books that has been studied left and right, inside and </span>
  <span id="freeText15104659426266499800" style="display:none">The Killer Inside Me is one of those novels that needs no introduction at all -- it is and will always be a classic of American noir fiction, it's been made into two movies (1976 and 2010), and chances are that if you haven't read the novel you've at least seen the film. Or, if you're really fainthearted, you've experienced neither, since both book and movie are dark, disturbing, and well past the point of unsettling. It's also one of those books that has been studied left and right, inside and out, and has even been the subject of a number of dissertations.<br /><br />This book is extremely difficult to read because of the sadistic, misogynistic violence (yes, I know ... a thing I generally try to avoid but I had to read this book -- it's a classic), but it's trying to untangle what's in Ford's mind that is really the draw for me. The novel is Lou's confession, if you will, his way of trying to make us understand the logic behind his actions, laying out his plans ahead of time for our perusal, and revealing just how he is able to fool people so easily -- until he can't any more. He is, in cliché speak, the ultimate wolf in sheep's clothing.<br /><br />There is so much to this novel aside from the violence, but going through everything I discovered in this book would take forever. As I said earlier, this novel has been scrutinized, studied, written about academically and otherwise, so there are a number of places to dig out more about it. It's up there among books that made me want to take a shower after reading it, but it's so damn good I just couldn't stop. And that sort of scares me, actually.<br /><br /> Insanely good, but to be very honest, I liked his <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19161888.Pop__1280" title="Pop. 1280 by Jim Thompson" rel="nofollow noopener">Pop. 1280</a> even more. <br /><br />much more here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.crimesegments.com/2016/12/the-killer-inside-me-by-jim-thompson_23.html">http://www.crimesegments.com/2016/12/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15104659426266499800" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1090888135" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1090888135" />
    <a title="Brandon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3214163-brandon"><img alt="Brandon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603283104p2/3214163.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1090888135?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brandon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brandon" href="/user/show/3214163-brandon">Brandon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316404068" href="/book/show/18129494-the-killer-inside-me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3214163-brandon?shelf=noir">noir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3214163-brandon?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3214163-brandon?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1090888135" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer97334795835411849">The threat of violence in the small Texas town profiled in Jim Thompson’s The Killer Inside Me is so low that the patrolling sheriff, Lou Ford, doesn't even need to carry a gun. Lou doesn't worry because hell, who’s more dangerous in Central City than good ol’ Lou himself? While he speaks in clichés and exudes a friendly demeanour, Lou’s true nature exists behind this social mask; a chilling homicidal maniac who could kill at any moment.<br/><br/>This was my first Jim Thompson and although the brutality o</span>
  <span id="freeText97334795835411849" style="display:none">The threat of violence in the small Texas town profiled in Jim Thompson’s The Killer Inside Me is so low that the patrolling sheriff, Lou Ford, doesn't even need to carry a gun. Lou doesn't worry because hell, who’s more dangerous in Central City than good ol’ Lou himself? While he speaks in clichés and exudes a friendly demeanour, Lou’s true nature exists behind this social mask; a chilling homicidal maniac who could kill at any moment.<br /><br />This was my first Jim Thompson and although the brutality of the violence and the pleasure Thompson’s Lou Ford receives in administering beatings and committing murder will stay with me for some time, the writing style kind of threw me off. I guess I haven’t read all that many West Texas noir novels and the language coupled with the manner of speaking came across as disjointed and difficult to identify with. Maybe it has something to do with being a Canadian living on the eastern seaboard born some thirty two years after this book was published. Who knows?<br /><br />I'm definitely interested in checking out more of Thompson’s work and perhaps giving this one a re-read sometime, after all it is only a few hundred pages. Stephen King writes the foreword (where he self admittedly rambles) and it’s listed as a crime classic with its influence reaching many of the top writers in the genre.<br /><br />Also posted @ <a href="http://everyreadthing.com/2014/11/07/the-killer-inside-me/" rel="nofollow noopener">Every Read Thing</a>.</span>

<div id="review_258270667" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/258270667" />
    <a title="Toby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5454475-toby"><img alt="Toby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542247337p2/5454475.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Toby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Toby" href="/user/show/5454475-toby">Toby</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780752851433" href="/book/show/11997.The_Killer_Inside_Me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5454475-toby?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5454475-toby?shelf=black-as-night">black-as-night</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5454475-toby?shelf=lit">lit</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer258270667" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8782906318850596814">Possibly even better than Pop. 1280, but essentially it's the same conceit - first person, unreliable narrator, manipulating his readers in to feeling sorry for him whilst going about his immoral business, in this case lots of cold blooded murder.<br/><br/>Fascinating and dark, Thompson grabs you with his tale of good ol' boy Lou Ford and you don't want to be let go, even when the house is burning up around you. Ford is more intelligent than everyone around him, but he has a dark secret in his past and a </span>
  <span id="freeText8782906318850596814" style="display:none">Possibly even better than Pop. 1280, but essentially it's the same conceit - first person, unreliable narrator, manipulating his readers in to feeling sorry for him whilst going about his immoral business, in this case lots of cold blooded murder.<br /><br />Fascinating and dark, Thompson grabs you with his tale of good ol' boy Lou Ford and you don't want to be let go, even when the house is burning up around you. Ford is more intelligent than everyone around him, but he has a dark secret in his past and a sickness in his head that has forced him to remain in his small town his whole life, hiding that cunning intellect by playing the fool. He needlessly ribs people by playing at the corny buffoon act, brow beating them with such humdingers as <i>"the way I look at it, a man doesn't get any more out of life that what he puts in to it,"</i> and <i>"it came to me out of a clear sky - the boy is the father to the man. Just like that, the boy is the father to the man."</i> <br /><br />It's got me wondering whether half of the people I have to deal with in my bookshop are secretly psychopathic killers out to wind me up or whether they are genuinely that much of a buffoon. And that's a completely separate wondering to 'just why was I identifying with that serial killer, is it because I too am a capable of such savage and uncaring violence?'<br /><br />It really makes a mockery of the hoopla surrounding Bret Easton Ellis to see such incendiary material of far superior literary quality without the bells and whistles being written so far in advance of American Psycho. <br /><br />I think this works as a fine companion piece to Charles Willeford's Pick-Up, but there's a chance that after reading both in quick succession you may want to take a holiday with unicorns and rainbows and long walks on the beach, that will of course be the overdose of prescription painkillers and gallons of hard liquor working on you after you decide that life isn't worth living anymore.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8782906318850596814" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_853593981" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/853593981" />
    <a title="Paul" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24437998-paul"><img alt="Paul" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479868929p2/24437998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/853593981?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul" href="/user/show/24437998-paul">Paul</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Readers of Pulp Fiction/ Hard Case Crime novels</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Paul by: </span>
      In introduction for a Richard Stark novel
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24437998-paul?shelf=crime-thrillers">crime-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24437998-paul?shelf=pulp-fiction">pulp-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer853593981" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7528269870559357976">'The Killer Inside Me' by Jim Thompson<br/><br/> This is my first experience of a Jim Thompson novel & if this is typical of his work, it won't be my last. <br/> I first came across Thompson whilst reading an introduction in one of Richard Stark's novels, who Stark cites as one of his influences & if you've read any of the 'Parker' novels you will notice a similar style to Thompson. <br/> Thompson himself admired Fyodor Dostoyevsky & critic/author Geoffrey O'Bren called Thompson the '"Dime-store Dostoyevsky." Whils</span>
  <span id="freeText7528269870559357976" style="display:none">'The Killer Inside Me' by Jim Thompson<br /><br /> This is my first experience of a Jim Thompson novel &amp; if this is typical of his work, it won't be my last. <br /> I first came across Thompson whilst reading an introduction in one of Richard Stark's novels, who Stark cites as one of his influences &amp; if you've read any of the 'Parker' novels you will notice a similar style to Thompson. <br /> Thompson himself admired Fyodor Dostoyevsky &amp; critic/author Geoffrey O'Bren called Thompson the '"Dime-store Dostoyevsky." Whilst comparison with Dostoyevsky may be a 'long bow to draw' there is no doubt they share some common attributes. Both draw vivid &amp; vibrant characters. Both authentically portray their respective eras in their use of language, social conditions &amp; cultural attitudes &amp; prejudices. What i love about Thompsons writing is that, of course, they were written in the era he sets his stories in. That touch of authenticity cannot be matched by modern writers, i don't believe.<br /> 'The Killer Inside Me' is told in the first person by Sheriff's Deputy Lou Ford, who to his fellow townspeople seems a likable, amiable, but somewhat dimwitted individual. This carefully cultivated facade masks a monster totally devoid of empathy for his fellow man or any 'normal' emotions we associate with what it is to be a human being.<br /> As a teenager, Ford assaults a young girl &amp; is caught by his older step brother, who for some inexplicable reason takes the blame &amp; is sent to prison. Upon his release, his brother gets a job in construction &amp; is killed on the job in mysterious circumstances. Ford blames the company's owner, Chester Conway, for his brother's death &amp; takes his revenge by killing Conway's son. <br /> Throughout this tale, Ford justifies his killing of Conway (&amp; other's) by claiming (to himself) that his victim's deaths were unavoidable &amp; somehow self defense. At one point though, during one of his many internal dialogues, he concedes he kills, because he likes it. That Deputy Lou Ford is a psychopath, there can be no doubt. You would expect Ford to have a head full of writhing serpents. But far from being the dimwit his fellow townsfolk think him to be, he is extremely intelligent. His every act is carefully considered &amp; ruthlessly executed.<br /> Things start to unravel for Ford when he realizes there may be one witness who can bring his carefully constructed 'house of cards' crashing down. But even staring defeat in the face, he manages, ever the manipulator, to…<br /><br /> If you like a great psychological thriller in the very best tradition of the Pulp Fiction/ Hard Case Crime genre, i urge you to read this. I give this 5 out of 5 stars.<br /><br />Good reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7528269870559357976" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1090190545" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1090190545" />

<div id="review_2238678157" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2238678157" />
    <a title="Mindi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6157592-mindi"><img alt="Mindi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538422738p2/6157592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2238678157?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mindi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mindi" href="/user/show/6157592-mindi">Mindi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316404068" href="/book/show/18129494-the-killer-inside-me">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2238678157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16844354634149664869">The Killer Inside Me is unlike any other book I've read. Published in 1952, it's a pulpy crime noir novel with a twist. The protagonist is no hard boiled detective hot on the trail of a killer, but rather the killer himself. Lou Ford is the Deputy Sheriff of a small town in Texas, and he's also a sociopathic murderer. And the reader gets to be inside his head for 229 pages. That's a very uncomfortable place to be. (Mild spoilers ahead, so if you want to go into this book knowing very little, sto</span>
  <span id="freeText16844354634149664869" style="display:none">The Killer Inside Me is unlike any other book I've read. Published in 1952, it's a pulpy crime noir novel with a twist. The protagonist is no hard boiled detective hot on the trail of a killer, but rather the killer himself. Lou Ford is the Deputy Sheriff of a small town in Texas, and he's also a sociopathic murderer. And the reader gets to be inside his head for 229 pages. That's a very uncomfortable place to be. (Mild spoilers ahead, so if you want to go into this book knowing very little, stop right here.)<br /><br />To be honest I'm astonished this book got published at all in 1952. There's a crudeness to it that surprised me every time Thompson wrote a sentence that had to be taboo for 1950's America. And yet, that crudeness is necessary at times, because we are in the mind of Lou Ford, and crudeness is quite at home there. Lou kills a number of people for varying reasons throughout the book, and he's fully convinced that no matter what he'll get away with it. Lou thinks he has everyone fooled, that's he's the nicest guy in Central City, but he soon becomes desperate and sloppy, and it doesn't take long for the rest of the sheriff's department to figure out what's really going on in town.<br /><br />Lou's attitude, his childhood, which is pieced together slowly through the novel, and his outlook on life are all very twisted. And his crimes are especially violent and disturbing, especially considering we have a front row seat for each and every one of them. Lou kills if he thinks it's necessary, and always to save his own hide. I won't go into the plot here, but it starts with a badly planned blackmail scheme and ends with Lou unraveling completely. <br /><br />The Killer Inside Me is a quick read that leaves you feeling like you need a palate cleanser book afterwards. Being inside the mind of Lou Ford is daunting and unpleasant, but this book left an impact on me that I know I won't soon forget.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16844354634149664869" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_916189179" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/916189179" />
    <a title="Joe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30725889-joe"><img alt="Joe" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/916189179?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joe" href="/user/show/30725889-joe">Joe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781407230054" href="/book/show/12308785-the-killer-inside-me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30725889-joe?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30725889-joe?shelf=read-again">read-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30725889-joe?shelf=transgressive">transgressive</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer916189179" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17009544861492343706">Did not get this at all. This sounded like my kind of thing, and with favourable reviews from Stanley Kubrick and Stephen King illuminating the front and back of the book, I figured that this would be right up my alley. But I was wrong. I was really disappointed. <br/><br/>There are a few scenes here that would have been shocking back in the day, no doubt. But they just don't quite live up to it today. However, I do appreciate that aspect of the book. What I did not appreciate was Jim Thompson's style of </span>
  <span id="freeText17009544861492343706" style="display:none">Did not get this at all. This sounded like my kind of thing, and with favourable reviews from Stanley Kubrick and Stephen King illuminating the front and back of the book, I figured that this would be right up my alley. But I was wrong. I was really disappointed. <br /><br />There are a few scenes here that would have been shocking back in the day, no doubt. But they just don't quite live up to it today. However, I do appreciate that aspect of the book. What I did not appreciate was Jim Thompson's style of writing. I generally love first-person narration, especially from sociopaths and people out on the fringes of society - but I could detect little merit in Thompson's writing. It was just dull, and to be quite frank, amateurish. <br /><br />The book really drags out, and is very confusing. Maybe its just me, but I was scratching my head at times and going back over pages trying to figure out who was who and what the hell was going on. The ending was a shambles. And that too, dragged out. If I was to recommend a book like this dictated in the first person by a sociopath, I would recommend <i>The Room</i> by Hubert Selby Jr. over this. That book has stood the passage of time, and probably always will, and is guaranteed to keep you awake at night.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17009544861492343706" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3498229?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nathan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nathan" href="/user/show/219312-nathan">Nathan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">crime and horror fans, lovers of great writing</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3498229" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17704362536329423020"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7621.Jim_Thompson' title='Jim Thompson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jim Thompson</a> worked on oil rigs in his youth. It's filthy, dangerous, deeply hair-raising work, all to get at something that's as precious as it is polluted. Reading his novels is surprisingly similar. His whiskey-soaked misogyny will make your skin crawl, but his ability to plumb the darkest corners of the human soul, with both skill and sympathy, is unmatched in literature.<br/><br/>This is the best Thompson book I've read by far, and one of the best books I've ever read for sheer narrative skill. His p</span>
  <span id="freeText17704362536329423020" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7621.Jim_Thompson" title="Jim Thompson" rel="nofollow noopener">Jim Thompson</a> worked on oil rigs in his youth. It's filthy, dangerous, deeply hair-raising work, all to get at something that's as precious as it is polluted. Reading his novels is surprisingly similar. His whiskey-soaked misogyny will make your skin crawl, but his ability to plumb the darkest corners of the human soul, with both skill and sympathy, is unmatched in literature.<br /><br />This is the best Thompson book I've read by far, and one of the best books I've ever read for sheer narrative skill. His protagonist here is one of fiction's great unreliable narrators, a charming, brilliant psychopath who knows exactly how sick he is, makes no excuses for it, and only dimly wishes he could stop. That fatalistic sense of resignation, and the narrator's undeniable charm in the midst of his truly hideous deeds, make this book an absolute tour de force.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17704362536329423020" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_42589'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/42589.Shoot_the_Piano_Player"><img alt="Shoot the Piano Player" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1328135504l/42589._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SNL+3/a3tz5/w2DpkPhkih2Nj+xFCYhghEyjYRSLSPGVhpVYVYexA6slPI7lB6H51adUuXWhdjSVhBKPt7h7jQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7621.Jim_Thompson">About Jim Thompson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/7621.Jim_Thompson"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1360741132p3/7621.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/7621.Jim_Thompson">Jim Thompson
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
1,772
followers
</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15788100360312145934"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/44217-master-list-of-author-disambiguation-by-spaces' rel='nofollow noopener'>See this thread for more information.</a></i> <br/><br/>James Myers Thompson was a United States writer of novels, short stories and screenplays, largely in the hardboiled style of crime fiction.<br/><br/>Thompson wrote more than thirty novels, the majority of which were original paperback publications by pulp fiction houses, from the lat</span>
  <span id="freeText15788100360312145934" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/44217-master-list-of-author-disambiguation-by-spaces" rel="nofollow noopener">See this thread for more information.</a></i> <br /><br />James Myers Thompson was a United States writer of novels, short stories and screenplays, largely in the hardboiled style of crime fiction.<br /><br />Thompson wrote more than thirty novels, the majority of which were original paperback publications by pulp fiction houses, from the late-1940s through mid-1950s. Despite some positive critical notice, notably by Anthony Boucher in the <i>New York Times</i>, he was little-recognized in his lifetime. Only after death did Thompson's literary stature grow, when in the late 1980s, several novels were re-published in the <i>Black Lizard</i> series of re-discovered crime fiction.<br /><br />Thompson's writing culminated in a few of his best-regarded works: <i>The Killer Inside Me, Savage Night, A Hell of a Woman</i> and <i>Pop. 1280</i>. In these works, Thompson turned the derided pulp genre into literature and art, featuring unreliable narrators, odd structure, and surrealism.<br /><br />The writer R.V. Cassills has suggested that of all pulp fiction, Thompson's was the rawest and most harrowing; that neither Dashiell Hammett nor Raymond Chandler nor even Horace McCoy, author of the bleak <i>They Shoot Horses, Don't They?</i>, ever "wrote a book within miles of Thompson". Similarly, in the introduction to Now and on Earth, Stephen King says he most admires Thompson's work because "The guy was over the top. The guy was absolutely over the top. Big Jim didn't know the meaning of the word stop. There are three brave lets inherent in the forgoing: he let himself see everything, he let himself write it down, then he let himself publish it."<br /><br />Thompson admired Fyodor Dostoevsky and was nicknamed "Dimestore Dostoevsky" by writer Geoffrey O'Brien. Film director Stephen Frears, who directed an adaptation of Thompson's The Grifters as 1990's <i>The Grifters</i>, also identified elements of Greek tragedy in his themes.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15788100360312145934" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
